  4. I'll have to preface this review by stating I never would have spent over $250+ on a shaver before (I've been a Mach 3/Mach 4 Turbo guy all my adult life) but after receiving this 'gratis' for review purposes, I'd have to say that when this shaver meets its maker, I WILL go out and buy another premium shaver (and will trust no brand except Philips Norelco). This gadget is like the iPhone (or Samsung Epic perhaps?) of the electric shaver world. The GyroFlex 3D technology that you've been seeing advertised on national TV these days is something truly worthy of the pub its been getting. Closest shave I've ever had, easy to clean (comes with a nice cleaning brush and a pouch for travel -- I use the pouch even when I'm not traveling -- and holds one heck of a charge). The LED display which notifies you how many minutes you have left before you need to recharge is bigger than the display on most alarm clocks! Smooth gliding, so easy to control, and oh so gentle on your skin. If you're the type of guy who hates to shave, this shaver is for you. I pray that if you're too stubborn to buy this for yourself that maybe you've got a special lady in your life who's sick of your 5 o'clock shadow and knows you've got a birthday coming up!<br /><br />Addendum (12/7/10): It has been asked what the benefits are for the model of shaver that is one step up from this one (the one you're looking at is the 2nd one from the top-of-line shaver in this series). From the comparison chart Amazon has provided, it appears the most expensive model also includes their patented Jet Clean system which is like a little tank that you store the shaver in overnight that cleans it and lubricates it by itself (you have to buy special solution for it). That seems like pretty impressive technology to me and I hope to one day be able to utilize it. It doesn't appear that Norelco sells a Jet Clean system on its own yet (sans shaver) but I would suggest they give it strong consideration in the near future.

(Took about twenty minutes to charge enough for sixty minutes of operation.)<br /><br />My husband hadn't used an electric shaver in years, preferring the closeness of a blade. However, after two weeks of use, he reports he gets a shave that rivals his blade razor. (Note: he does not have a heavy beard.) He likes that the shaving heads are flexible, enabling him to access areas that before were difficult with the old style electric shavers. He also likes that it comes with a case so he can take the charged shaver to the gym. Clean-up is easy: just run the heads under warm water and let them dry. A brush gets any residue left in the heads.<br /><br />So far, no face irritation, a common complaint with many electric shavers. Another plus is that he can use the shaver wet or dry.<br /><br />The only negative thing might be that the shaver cannot be used with a cord; you must charge it as needed.<br /><br />Another reviewer noted that the shaver goes into lock mode when moved. This hasn't been a problem for us.<br /><br />It should be noted that the directions say not to charge the shaver more than sixty minutes. So, be sure to unplug it after the allotted charge time so as to preserve battery life. Heads are costly to replace. By following cleaning instruction, you should avoid problems with head life.<br /><br />Overall, the best electric razor my husband has used. A strong two thumbs up for the Philips Norelco 1290x/40 SensoTouch 3d Electric Shaver.
  6. The big question on this razor really isn't \\"Is this a good razor?\\" but rather \\"What do I get for spending $230+?\\". This is Norelco's premium model. As such, you're getting the most advanced heads, premium construction, longest lasting battery, and longest warranty.<br /><br />Overall, if you don't need:<br />*metal construction,<br />*a super-long battery,<br />*a touch screen on/off button, or the<br />*digital minute display,<br />then you can opt for the less expensive 3-d model. From there it's a step down to the 2-d flexing heads. After that you make a choice between the Nivea wet shavers or the SpeedXL system. All are quite capable, but this model combines the best from all of those.<br /><br />You'll definitely get the best, most comfortable shave from this one and will benefit from wet or dry shaving.<br /><br />My personal experience is based on years of using Norelco razors. I've been using a SpeedXL razor for the past 4 years. It replaced the bottom-end $40 Norelco I had before that. The SpeedXL was a comfort improvement over the basic model, and the 3D system is yet another improvement over the SpeedXL. I had always wanted to try one of the Nivea/wet style shavers and now this model lets me use any shave gel, not just the Nivea cartridges. I've been getting the best dry shave ever, and once my skin got adjusted, it really is *almost* as close as a blade. Using it in the shower gets even closer. At first, I think I was misusing it because it glides so easily and conforms to your face so well, that I was probably pushing too hard thinking it was like my old razor. This one works well with a very light touch.<br /><br />What differentiates this model from other Norelcos:<br />===================================================<br /><br />Advanced heads:<br />---------------<br />Norelco razors come in many flavors, with each series using different heads. To be clear, each razor which uses the same replacement head will perform similarly, and the difference in price is simply due to the other features. On this model (which is part of the 12xx series), that means a metal construction body, touch-screen control vs. a hard button, and the digital minute display vs. a bar graph.<br /><br />The difference between heads (12xx series, 11xx series, etc) is the amount of flex, the degree of flexion, and the pressure it takes to actually flex the heads. On this model, the heads are VERY easy to flex and move in all directions. This leads to less pressure against your face when shaving, fewer strokes because the heads can reach more angles at once, and both of those lead to less irritaion. The foils are similar to the Speed XL (my previous model), in that they have 3 different slot types, but only two cutting paths vs. 3 on the SpeedXL. I definitely like these heads better. They seem to do a better job of letting the hairs into the cutters.<br /><br />3D models are the 12xx series and use the RQ12 heads.<br />2D models are the 11xx series and use the RQ11 heads.<br />Arcitect models seem to be discontinued, but are the 10xx series and use the RQ10 heads.<br />SpeedXL models use the HQ9 heads, and cannot be used in the shower or for wet shaving.<br />I'm not sure if any of the heads are interchangeable.<br /><br />Premium Construction:<br />---------------------<br />The metal body and rubberized back are really nice. Only the front face is plastic, and on this model, not even the button sticks out or moves. The look is sleek, clean, and cool. It truly feels like a quality razor. Not that this really affects performance, but it does give confidence in its durability. The construction on this series allows for both wet and dry shaving. With wet shaving, you can also use shaving foam or gel. This is a big benefit to those who shave in the shower, or who prefer lotion. Since you can use any kind you like, this may save money over using Norelco's Nivea models, which use specialized packages of the Nivea gel. The razor is quieter than other models, and has more of a higher pitch making it sound like the heads really spin faster.<br /><br />Longest battery:<br />----------------<br />Provides up to 60 minutes of shaving, and only takes 60 minutes to charge. Very convenient, and the charging stand is useful, too. Other models provide as little as 30-50 minutes on a full charge. Given the speed of the cut from this model, plus the long life, you could likely pack this for a week long trip without hesitation. The downside is that it can ONLY be charged in the stand - there is no way to plug the adapter directly into the razor itself. As such, the pouch is not large enought to fit the razor, stand and power cord. So longer trips require more space to pack the stand. Additionally the razor and pouch is larger than lower end models, so even taking just the razor will require a bit more space. The battery is Li-ion, so it should stand up well over time.<br /><br />Longest Warranty:<br />-----------------<br />2 full years.<br /><br />Bead/sideburn trimmer:<br />----------------------<br />It slides our vs. flips out and is narrower than the lower end models. However, it has finer teeth and is much more effective in my opinion. A clear improvement over the past. The problem with the trimmer on this model is that the main shaving heads often block your view of the trimmer, so it is more difficult to see it.<br /><br />Criticisms:<br />===========<br />-Price. Obviously, this model is up to twice as much as other Norelco's. I don't think you get twice the performance.<br />-Charging. I don't like that you have to use the stand to charge it. If you don't have space on your sink, or if it's a rough surface, you'll have more of a pain to charge it. Also, for travel purposes, long trips require you take the charging stand. Lastly, the charging port on the stand is on the right-hand side vs. being centered in the back. For those like me, where the outlet is to the left of where the stand sits, this looks a bit messy with the cord going to the opposite side.<br />-Smaller stubble collection - each head stores the stubble vs all of it being collected together. To clean, you have to flip open each of the three heads. It's not hard, but more work than a simply single-button press on the older shavers.<br /><br />Overall Assessment:<br />===================<br />For the criticisms, mostly the price and charging, I'm deducting 1-star. I believe this is the best Norelco you can buy, but for this price it's hard to justify not being absolutely perfect. I don't think those should necessarily deter you to a different brand or model. They may not be issues to you, and surely some of the features of this model may well outweigh the criticisms I have. You'll have to find the sweet spot of price/features for yourself.eally spin faster. Longest battery: ---------------- Provides up to 60 minutes of shaving, and only takes 60 minutes to charge.   30. The Philips Norelco 1290x SensoTouch 3D electric shaver is Philip's top of the line electric shaver. As such, it commands a high price tag, but if you typically like to purchase flagship items the Philips makes you feel like you got your money's worth.<br /><br />The design of the SensoTouch 3D is what sets this shaver apart from cheaper models. Just picking the shaver up and feeling its heft and quality construction tells you where a good deal of the money went. It's finished with a soft touch ribbed back and the front has a piano black finish beneath which hides the shaver's electronic display. There is a chrome band around the front of the shaver that appears to actually be made of metal.<br /><br />The power button is the only button on the shaver and is touch sensitive. When the shaver is moved (it must have an internal motion sensor) lighted rings illuminate around the power button so you can locate it easily. The electronic display shows the minutes of shave time remaining (up to 60 minutes), a cleaning indicator, an auto-lock indicator, a replace shaver heads indicator, a low battery indicator, and a jammed heads indicator.<br /><br />The shaving heads are perched on the top and pivot inward and outward individually of each other. There's just enough tension in the shaver heads to keep them in contact with various facial contours, but not too much as to cause undue irritation. The round heads have three different shaving rings. The outermost edge is for normal stubble, the next ring is for longer hairs, and the center ring is for shorter stubble. Additionally, on the left hand side of the Philips is a sliding switch that extends a small trimmer from right behind the shaver's head.<br /><br />Included with the Philips is a charging stand. The stand holds the shaver upright and charges it through two small metal nubs located on the left and right hand side of the shaver. The charging stand can complete a charge in one hour or a quick charge in 5 minutes for 3 minutes of shave time. Also included with the shaver is a zippered travel pouch, a plastic cap for the shave head, and a cleaning brush.<br /><br />The SensoTouch is very quiet in operation and provides a close shave without irritation, even on my sensitive skin. My neck is a little pink afterwards but it fades away quickly. I liked the fact that the heads pivoted outward individually since it meant I could leave only one of the heads in contact with my face and was then able to shave around my goatee more precisely. Another thing I liked was that fact that if I let my beard grow for a day or two (because I can be lazy) it still shaved very closely without snagging on any hairs. I'd like to mention that the Philips can be used with shaving cream as well for an even closer shave, but I never felt the need to do so since it worked very well when used dry. To clean out the shaver heads you simply tip each one back and run the shaver's head under hot water. You can also disassemble the heads completely and clean them with the included brush.<br /><br />The only negatives I have are as follows: 1) Make sure you either rinse the shaver head out after every use or don't lay it on its side. When you do so shavings fall out of the shaver head and onto the counter. 2) The only way to charge to shaver is with the charging stand so you can't plug it in and use it. It does have a quick charge feature but sometimes I am in a rush and being able to use it right away would be better. 3) There is no travel lock to disable the power button. It does have an \\"automatic travel lock\\" that turns on when the shaver is moved around for 5 minutes and not used, but to turn the automatic lock off all you have to do is press the power button. That seems silly to me. I will admit that the power button takes a firm press to engage so it's probably not much of an issue. 4) There are little \\"water spots\\" under the front display that were present when I took the shaver outof the box.<br /><br />All in all... Nicely made, closely shaves, the Rolex of shavers.ly shaves, the Rolex of shavers.

I was once away from home without the charger for a week in Las Vegas. It never failed to operate normally and with vigor from day one through day seven. The charge remaining never went below 50%<br /><br />It's a welcome return to the world of electric shavers for me after my sudden searing departure.   41. Note: I shave my whole head, so the Norelco is the only one that works well over the lumps. This top-of-the-line Norelco is great -- shaving in under 20 minutes what took 30+ minutes with my (good) 3-yr-old Norelco. It's quiet, fast, close, and a larger overall surface area. Great design that's easy to clean, plus a count-down timer (versus charge meter) on the highest-level model (and 60-minute charge vs. 50 minutes). If you travel take note -- the design team couldn't leave great engineering alone... The charging cord could easily fit the bottom of the shaver, but instead, it plugs into a Y-shaped charging stand, so the shaver stands upright while charging (via two small knobs on either side). So if you travel, you need to take this large, flimsy, odd-shaped charging stand with you in addition to the simple cord. Also, there's a beautiful motion-activated moving circular light around the \\"on\\" switch. Whenever you touch the thing, it starts going, so I wonder if a 12-hour car trip would have this thing lighting the whole time -- probably not much of a battery drain, but still annoying. Overall, a great, efficient shaver (worth 2x the cheaper models, if you can easily afford it), with an attractive, easy-to-clean design, but a bit-too-egotistical design team wanting you to display it like a work of art.

The countdown (minutes left) feature works well.<br /><br />Shaving works well but it is a mixed result too. This shaver is huge- much more than I realized when I bought it. The floating platform is large too. The theory that the floating platform will work better than the floating heads alone seems not to be true. Because of the size, the shaver shaves fairly quickly and perhaps slightly better on large flat areas, but struggles on sharp curves - thus better or worse than my 9190 depending on the curve. Both shavers work noticeably worse than the Norelco triple head shavers of decades ago. I agree with another reviewer that said that Norelco's biggest competition is its own past.<br /><br />This shaver has turned out not to be suitable for travel. On previous Norelco shavers I could plug the cord directly into the shaver- far more convenient. This clumsy and ill-fitting charger stand is too bulky to drag around. Also, inexplicably, this high-end model has no lock. The manual is confused on this point, contradicting itself. The shaver turns out to be confused too; if I hold it just right sometimes I can activate the lock feature, even though the lock symbol (which they claim is on this unit) doesn't come on. Then it acts locked, then later isn't. Bizarre. Is this an unfixed mistake they simply decided to document as not being implemented instead of deciding to fix?<br /><br />I can't resist an editorial comment. I am a veteran executive with big corporate experience. This product is what happens when marketing departments design products, trying to impress the board with gee-whiz looks, and lose track of the engineering wisdom and direct customer feedback (i.e. not funneled through a self-serving consultant). The cool things on previous products disappear, obvious functionality is missing, various impracticalities creep in, the main purpose is somewhat impaired, or even very impaired. As a consumer it's frustrating; it so easily could be better. This shaver strikes me as a product of such a process. For example the sideburn trimmers were better far back in time and have gradually declined.<br /><br />Still, this shaver isn't so bad I am discarding it and I use it now as my regular home shaver. I hope the next one I buy will be back on track.<br /><br />Pros:<br />Has countdown minutes remaining which I find very valuable.<br />Charges surprisingly quickly, at least now being new.<br />Shaves large flat areas quickly.<br /><br />Cons:<br />Has trouble shaving on curved skin surfaces, such as a jaw line.<br />Charger platform from hell, very bulky, cord won't go directly into shaver, shaver seating in charger takes a nudge or two sometimes to contact.<br />Much harder to clean heads than my previous models. Hard to open shaver heads; kludgy latch, hard to operate, have to open each separately, heads keep wanting to close while trying to clean, hard to knock shavings out without using water, shaver appears only partly protected from water.<br />Lock feature on lower models missing on this high-end model.<br />Large size less convenient for travel.<br />Sideburn trimmer works poorly and is very very loud. The new head design is huge and gets in the way when trying to trim.

  55. Having previously used Norelco's Arcitec 1090 high-end shaver, I was anxious to try out the SensoTouch 3D. This is a great looking product, really well designed. For anyone who likes gadgets, this is definitely a shaver you may want to consider. Of course, it takes more than a cool design to be worth the price tag. I have been using this unit for the past few weeks and am totally satisfied with the shave I get. The older Arcitec model was my first electric shaver, and I haven't wanted to go back to the disposable blades I used to use. My older model was still getting the job done after about two years of use, so I'd say Norelco makes a durable product. Hopefully I will be saying the same about the 1290 SensoTouch a couple years from now. The shaver does deliver on the promise of a very close shave - for me, its nearly identical to what I'm accustomed to with a disposable razor. This unit can be used for a wet or dry shave. I prefer wet, but I tried dry just to see if it irritated my skin - it did not. A huge plus was much quieter operation. Even though I got used to it over time, the Arcitec model was kind of overly loud. The SensoTouch is very quiet. Over-charging the battery is a potential issue to be aware of. I say that because once charged, the shaver is not supposed to be left charging. For instance, an electric toothbruth or a cell phone can be plugged into a charger long after the battery is fully revived. Not the case here. It only takes about an hour to achieve a full charge, but at that point the directions are very clear that leaving it on the charger all the time will lessen the battery life. I'm not about to take a chance. So charge it fully and unplug it. The charge will last about one hour, which I have easily managed a week's worth of shave on. Your mileage will vary of course. The unit is not designed to be used plugged in. If the shaver's charge has expired, you will need to pop it back on the charger and wait for it to build up somejuice. Best plan that works for me is charge it once a week, just getting used to needing to it. The downside to this is that, since the battery cannot be replaced, you will not be able to run the shaver on AC power after the battery ceases to hold a charge. The digital display provides a reading of how many minutes are left before needing a charge. Very handy.

You'd hope, behind the great industrial design, the actual shave would be better by leaps and bounds. It's not. The core shaving performance is remarkably unimproved; and several design have made it less convenient than ever before. I like Norelco, I recommend that brand, but you can get a much less expensive model with equal performance. While the motor feels a bit more powerful and the shaving heads are slightly redesign; in real life tests the time it took to shave and the closeness of the shave was more or less the same. More importantly, while shaving above the jawline is a cinch; shaving around the neck had always been a 1 star out of 10 performance for Norelco and continues to be so. If you watch the promotional videos they advocate for circular motions; however ultimately this seems to be more of a distraction which forces you to go directly against the grain - and I have found this is really the only way to make progress however it leads to skin cuts and soreness. You could go down or straight across the neck 20 times with little to show even with the supposedly improved cutting heads. It's not worse that the older 8000 model, it's just not better. While core shaving performance hasn't changed, Norelco seems committed to make several features worse off: *The feeble straight trimmer is even more useless - I would say it is 80% worse now * This design requires cleaning the heads after every use. This is a major pain and a huge step backwards particularly because the debris inevitably ends up getting splashing around the sink and rather than have this happen twice a month, now it occurs every day. Furthermore the heads now need to dry out every day which means you wouldn't want to store this in a closed / unventilated space. If you don't clean it every day the debris just falls out because it is not a sealed space. * You need the bulky stand to charge it (why didn't they just let you plug into the razor directly for when you travel?) * It appears to have very elementary charging logic and so you need to watch it and unplug it after a short amount of time * The box is gigantic and wasteful - negative points for eco-friendly packaging And the #1 most useless feature... it has a movement detector which is so incredibly sensitive that it lights up the buttons even if you are closing the door or flushing the toilet. Fantastic engineering for sure... and I can only guess that the LCD screen is 40% of the hardware cost... but all it does is wear down your battery.

This is now my 4th high end Norelco. It does sadden me however, that when the battery on this shaver no longer charges, it will either be a monument or a throw away item. MUCH quieter than any foil shaver in operation - can be of major importance for spouse or partner.<br />- Cleaning station (Jet Clean) is quieter too; in fact, after the first 4 minutes or so, it is completely silent.<br />- Cleaning solution has a light, pleasant scent; Panasonic cartridges are less so (more like old soap)<br />- Cleaning station works with all 3D models, unlike Panasonic [[ASIN:B002N5MHLK Panasonic ES-LA93-K Vortex Men's Shaver]].<br />- Lightweight (at least it feels lighter than my Braun or Panasonic).<br />- Uniform cutting; not as close as a foil, and definitely takes more time and effort for your skin to condition (you will likely need the full 21 days recommended by Norelco), but fewer patches of longer/shorter whiskers than with a foil.<br /><br />Cons<br />- As above, not as close as a foil, although with time could be very similar.<br />- Initially more irritating to the skin (YMMV).<br />- \\"Liquid Zinc\\" metal trim is actually some sort of metal instead of chrome-colored plastic, so is fairly durable, but it does seem to be picking up tarnish; stainless steel polish seems to help, but not encouraging for something used and stored wet<br />- The on/off \\"touch\\" button on this model is particularly squirrelly, and I couldn't get it to turn on until I had put it in the charger several times and fiddled with the heads (go figure). No travel lock function as far as I can tell, but it really doesn't need one with the design - you need a human touch to turn it on. I've used a 1280x for awhile, and it's definitely a more positive and reliable function to press a real button.<br />- Cleaning solution for Jet Clean needs more frequent change than cartridge (but I suspect is more sanitary because of).<br /><br />Over all, I like it, other than the one unit dead on arrival. The front is a clean, smooth surface, and (theoretically) less apt to have switch problems (except as noted); the silver \\"On\\" logo on my 1280x has already worn off after just a couple of weeks; I expect the Norelco/Model banner to follow shortly. Time will tell, and I'm getting used to the rotary experience again (used Norelcos years ago). Nice thing about these models is that you can use them wet, and I shave with a gel which (for me) provides less irritation. About the same shaving time as with a foil, but a much quieter experience. I think it's worth it.<br /><br />Postscript: I have discovered the (undocumented) secret of success with turning this shaver on and off! Because of the unique \\"power saving\\" function, the shaver \\"knows\\" when it is moved. If it senses movement but is not turned on for five minutes, it goes into \\"lock\\" mode - a flashing lock symbol appears on the front of the shaver when it is moved. If you keep it relatively still and press the power button, it will never come on. It requires gentle motion while touching the power symbol to reactivate it, and the same in unlocked mode - you will note that the switch light goes out when it is motionless. Move the shaver, and voila! the switch is outlined by the flashing ring, and can be turned on. Technology is our own worst enemy....hile, and it's definitely a more positive and reliable function to press a real button. - Cleaning solution for Jet Clean needs more frequent change than cartridge (but I suspect is more sanitary because of). The one quibble I have with the package is the travel situation. The Senso Touch, like the Arcitec, must be charged in the stand; you can't plug it in directly. This is a design choice which allows the units to be sealed against water. No problem. But the Arcitec came with a travel case which also allowed charging. It is a hard case that accepted the charger plug and charged the unit when inside the case. The Senso Touch comes with a soft pouch that does not permit charging. So your only choice is the stand. The stand does not fit into the soft pouch for travel, so if you are going on a longer trip and will need to recharge the shaver while away from home, you will need to bring the stand. It is awkward to pack and is made of plastic. Pack it carefully. This not a problem on short trips when you will not use up the 60 minutes or so of battery power. For me this is 10-14 days, and I have taken longer trips than that. I do recommend this shaver. It is the best shave this side of a blade. I have used it both wet and dry. Frankly not much difference in the results, but good to have options. Four stars only because of the travel charging issue, performance is five stars.

When I received the SensoTouch 3D I figured that I would give it a try, but that the real litmus test would be with my husband as he is the \\"worst case scenario\\" on which to test any hair removal product.<br /><br />My husband is Mediterranean/Italian and has copious amounts of coarse dark hair. The Bald Guy said that if he shaves his head super close with a razor, the immediate SensoTouch result is similar to the next day after shaving with a regular blade. Which, isn't bad, considering his wiry, coarse hair.<br /><br />But it isn't faster. If it had been faster to use the SensoTouch, he would have loved it and would have accepted not-quite-razor-close results in the name of efficiency. As is, it took him around the same amount of time to shave his head and face with the SensoTouch as it did with a safety razor. The one plus about this electric razor is that it is very gentle and low vibration on the face, producing minimal irritation- so in an \\"oops I overslept\\" situation, he can use this to tidy his face a little bit, but still not with the crisp, cleanness provided by a more traditional safety razor. The SensoTouch really hugged my facial curves and the three heads took care of my fuzz in a couple of passes. I looked with my magnifying mirror and my skin was smooth and hairless.   163. I recently purchased this shaver with some trepidation, and my joys and fears both materialized. The problems are very annoying: First, the trimmer is seriously flawed because it is nearly impossible to trim and see what you are trimming because the overall size of the shaving head interferes with the shaver's visualization of the area being trimmed. Second, I don't understand why a \\"stand\\" is needed for charging. I travel a lot and love a battery powered device, but hate having to carry a stand (I knew this when I purchased it because I wanted the better shave of a top level Norelco, but I still hate the stand). In this day and age, it would seem that a simple cord directly from the shaver to a wall plug could be designed while accommodating 120 and 240 ac/dc, and that it could be designed with all the electronics inside the shaver to avoid all the extra paraphenalia you are forced to travel with including extra large plugs assemblies (as Norelco used to do routinely). Finally, the overall size of this new shaver seems excessively large, including the overall size of the head with its 3 rotating blades. Is all that extra head casing really needed in the design? In fact, this new model takes up easily twice the space of lesser models in my toiletry bag.

The extremely small trimmer was for me the biggest disappointment because it does not do a very good or very fast job on my side burns. Much has been made in some previous reviews about being careful not to overcharge the battery. On my razor, the charging of the battery stops after the battery is fully charged. I know this because both the power adapter and the shaver cool-off after &#34;60&#34; minutes is reached. Furthermore, the if the charging didn't stop, or at least diminish to a trickle charge, the battery would at the very least overheat, if not explode or catch fire. No where in my owner's manual is there a warning not to overcharge the battery by leaving the shaver plugged in. Again, I have the 1290x and its manual, so I am not speaking about other models. I will say, however, that my Spectra is exactly the same way; it stops charging when the battery is fully charged. I will continue to use my Spectra while traveling, however, for two reasons. First, the 1290x travel case is inadequate in my opinion to protect the razor in a suit case. Second, should the 1290x battery fail while I'm traveling, I would not be able to shave because I can't plug the cord directly into the razor like I can with the Spectra. I understand that Philips wanted to make sure that none of the shaver's users would be accidentally electrocuted by shaving in the shower with a plugged-in razor, but I don't want to have to travel with a back-up razor. UPDATE I no longer have this razor because the LED display failed during the warranty period and Philips replaced the defective handle with what they said was a &#34;new&#34; handle. Seven months later, and one month longer than itswarranty, the second handle stopped working completely. Philips offered me a 15 percent discount coupon on a new unit. I took the handle apart and found that the battery still had full power (3.7 volts), so I know that the battery was not the issue. Interestingly, I noticed that the 8000-series shavers were discontinued and a new 9700-series shaver has come out. Since the 9700-series uses the same heads as the 8000-series did, I decided to purchase a new S9721/84 so that I can use the two sets of heads that I purchased as spares for the 1290x. Also, even though I wanted to give a Braun series-9 shaver a try, my research showed that not only have Braun's customer service and products been no better nor more reliable than that of Philips, their series-9 shavers are neither sold nor supported in the US. I'll find out soon enough if the 1290x model was a lemon or a harbinger of the things to come from Philips Norelco.

  205. I have owned a few electric shavers in the past that claim to offer a genuinely close shave / wet shave replacement. But nothing has ever really matched a Gillette 5 blade shave.<br /><br />The Philips 1290 is about as close as I have got - it cuts incredibly close and quickly and in my opinion is probably the first electric shaver that can truly claim to be a wet shave replacement.<br /><br />It cuts short, long hair equally as well - both dry and wet (in the shower). I haven't tried it with shaving foam yet, but the instructions state that you can.<br /><br />The shaver itself is incredibly well made. Magnesium / rubber housing feels sturdy, doesn't creek when flexing to the contours of your face etc. The motor is quite, the touch sensitive start button responsive and they have obviously put a lot of time and effort into the user interface, as its clear and looks great.<br /><br />many reviews don't really touch upon this, but Philips have finally got the weight right. There shavers in the past have either suffered from being to light or heavy, but the balance of the 1290 is just right.<br /><br />The built hair trimmer is good - but I don't use it that much.<br /><br />It is expensive...but you get what you pay for. If you shave every day its well worth the investment in the top of line Philips. I have read that some people have had some issues with the battery dieing - my advice is check the electrical specification if outside the US. Charging a lithium-ion battery from a different power source will kill the battery or degrade it.<br /><br />Easily hands down the best electric shaver I have ever owned.
